I figured i would try the Pro-Dental instead of getting another Dentek since the reviews for the new denteks are terrible.<br /><br />So my main concern with these Pro-Dental guards is that they would be too soft and I'd chew them apart quickly. And that is yet to be determined. However, i have recently woken up realizing i was just grinding my teeth on the night guard during vivid dreams. (Pretty weird feeling!). And yes, so far the soft plastic is holding up well. I hope they continue to endure.<br /><br />Molding experience:<br />I found before molding i needed to trim the material on the top (so it wasn't so deep dish) and i needed to leave in the hot water 1 second longer to get a good squishy/workable consistency for custom molding to my mouth. DO NOT be affraid of putting the mouth piece in your mouth after taking it out of the hot water. Just let it air cool for 5 seconds and get it in your mouth. It will be very warm, but not hot.<br /><br />I tried molding one without trimming it at all and the material squished across the entire roof of my mouth, and cooled to form something that looked more like one of those plastic orthodontic retainers you get after your braces come off. Needless to say it was still soft but not comfortable as it felt like my tongue had no room in my mouth. I suppose i could &#34;return&#34; this oneand request another piece be sent, but for the price of these 3, I do not feel it is necessary. It is still usable and will serve well as a backup i can keep in my luggage all the time in case i forget to pack the regular use one.<br /><br />Comfort:<br />The two that i trimmed properly are very comfortable in my mouth. I usually start using it as i read a book in bed before falling asleep and after 5 minutes i forget it's in my mouth. However when i do bite down i'm still adjusting to the feeling of my front teeth being able to bite into the soft plastic as apposed to the hard plastic of the Dentek. And i guess that's why i question the longevity of this product.<br /><br />Cleaning tip:<br />One very important instruction included in the package is to NOT USE MOUTHWASH to clean these platic detal appliances. Mouthwash will dry out the plasic and it will crumble. Just use regular hand soap or basic toothpaste. I think that's why my Dentek lasted longer than everybody writing bad reviews, i have always used a soft brush and mild hand soap to clean it every morning.<br />Hope this helps.

  388. I think these are identical to the $2 EVA guards you can find elsewhere on Amazon. What you are paying for is the service (see below). Also, they will send you additional guards if you screw up.<br /><br />This is significantly bulkier than the night guard that my dentist made 20 years ago. The walls of the guard (inside, outside, bottom) are thick (~3 mm after fitting) and I felt like I was wearing a sports mouthguard. Overcoming this is hard: I had to squeeze all three surfaces of the guard against my teeth using my fingers. This will take considerably longer than the 5 second window you have after taking the guard out of the boiling water. It took me about 8 rounds of molding. And then trim the elongated tops of the walls. And it still won't be thin. (If you ask Don to thin them (see below), don't bother trying to thin the walls yourself when molding it - just make a simple impression and let Don do all the thinning.)<br /><br />In addition to the thick walls, it's really not clear why the trough for your teeth is so wide. Almost no one has teeth that wide. And you're softening the guard anyways, so if the trough were made narrower and happened to be narrower than your teeth, it would just stretch when you molded it.<br /><br />I didn't have any problem with the softened curling walls sticking together, as the instructions warns, and I don't think it's that important how you position the hot guard on the counter (and you can probably skip the wet paper towel, too). However, the guard still has to cool down enough to put in your mouth. And be sure to shake out all the hot water before putting in your mouth.<br /><br />UPDATE<br />Don Closson at ProDental was very solicitous about my concerns. He called me at home offering to thin the impression at his lab for no additional charge. I'm excited to see how this will turn out. Stay tuned...<br /><br />3-MONTH UPDATE<br />I actually sent it back a second time to be thinned even more - I told Don to go as thin as possible. After that it wasn't bad - still thicker than a dentist-made guard, but not bad. Don wanted to keep the occlusal face somewhat thicker so that I wouldn't wear through it. To give you an idea of how thin they are after the second thinning, with my mouth closed someone might not be able to tell that I'm wearing them. The thinned surface had a cat's tongue texture, which initially was annoying, but it's smoothed over time and I no longer notice it.<br /><br />When I'm awake, I find that I clench my teeth when wearing the guard. I think this is because the occlusal face is somewhat thick and because they are compressible. My front teeth have cut a little into the guard so that it sits a little higher on my gums, but it's not a big deal.<br /><br />At the same time I got a SISU SOVA night guard. I was very hopeful about these because they are thin, hard, and can be remolded from scratch. Also, they mold at a lower temperature and with more working time than EVA. To give you a sense of how thin they are, with your mouth closed no one could tell that you were wearing them. However, they contract slightly as they harden and I found them extremely difficult to get a precise fit (I tried over 40 times with two different guards). I have given up on wearing these and prefer the EVA.

You can mold this mouth guard to fit your teeth perfectly very easily! You simply boil water, take the pot off the heat source, put the guard in, watch it until it starts to fold (about 19 seconds for me) take it out with a spoon, let it sit on a paper towel for a few seconds until it cools off, then put it in your mouth! Once in your mouth you close your lips and suck all the air in to make the guard conform to the front of your teeth, while doing this you must also push on the inside with your tongue and push with your fingers on your cheeks.
